# Fault Localization: HDA Intel Sound Fails After Suspend to RAM

- **Repository**: github.com/sg-evals/linux--07c4ee00 (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/linux--07c4ee00 (mirror of torvalds/linux)
- **Kernel Version**: 3.7.6
- **Difficulty**: expert
- **Category**: fault_localization
- **Subsystem**: Drivers
- **Component**: Sound (HDA Intel)

## Bug Report

**Bug ID**: 53441
**Summary**: hda_intel: sound stops working after suspend to ram
**Regression**: Yes (works on v3.6.11, broken since v3.7.1)

On a fresh boot the sound card works fine. After a few suspends to ram (it doesn't necessarily happen after just one) the sound card stops working well. The sound comes out choppy, as a series of clicks separated by 2 second or so silences.

I see these messages in the kernel log right after resume:
```
hda-intel: azx_get_response timeout, switching to polling mode: last cmd=0x00170503
hda-intel: No response from codec, disabling MSI: last cmd=0x00170503
hda_intel: azx_get_response timeout, switching to single_cmd mode: last cmd=0x00170503
```

The only way to fix the sound seems to be a reboot. I don't have this problem with v3.6.11, it appeared with kernel v3.7.1 (I have not tested v3.7). Right now I'm running 3.7.6 and the problem is still there.

```
$ lspci | grep -i audio
00:1b.0 Audio device: Intel Corporation 5 Series/3400 Series Chipset High Definition Audio (rev 05)
01:00.1 Audio device: NVIDIA Corporation High Definition Audio Controller (rev a1)

$ lsmod | grep snd
snd_hda_codec_hdmi     24993  4
snd_hda_codec_idt      54740  1
snd_hda_intel          24840  6
snd_hda_codec          71155  3 snd_hda_codec_hdmi,snd_hda_codec_idt,snd_hda_intel
snd_pcm                74322  3 snd_hda_codec_hdmi,snd_hda_codec,snd_hda_intel
snd_page_alloc          7333  2 snd_pcm,snd_hda_intel
snd_timer              17563  1 snd_pcm
```

## Task

You are a fault localization agent. Given the bug report above, your task is to identify the **exact source file(s)** and **function(s)/data structure(s)** in the Linux kernel source tree (at `/workspace`) that need to be modified to fix this bug.

You must:
1. Analyze the bug report to understand the symptoms and context
2. Search the kernel source code to identify the relevant subsystem and files
3. Narrow down to the specific file(s) and function(s)/data structure(s) that contain the bug or need modification
4. Write your findings to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json` in the following format:

```json
{
  "buggy_files": ["path/to/file.c"],
  "buggy_functions": ["function_or_struct_name"],
  "confidence": 0.8,
  "reasoning": "Brief explanation of why these locations are the fault"
}
```

**Important**: Paths should be relative to the kernel source root (e.g., `kernel/sched/core.c`, not `/workspace/kernel/sched/core.c`).

## Success Criteria

- [ ] Correctly identify the buggy file(s)
- [ ] Correctly identify the buggy function(s) or data structure(s)

On resume, azx_init_chip() is called and checks 'if (!chip->single_cmd)' before reinitializing CORB/RIRB (line 1222). This causes subsequent codec communication timeouts and the error messages observed. The fix is to reset the single_cmd, polling_mode, and poll_count flags immediately after calling azx_reset() in azx_init_chip(), ensuring that after a hardware reset, the driver returns to normal CORB/RIRB mode. This is a regression introduced between kernel 3.6.11 and 3.7.1 where these software state flags were not properly managed across suspend/resume cycles."

90-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed the fault localization analysis. Let me provide a summary:

## Summary

I've successfully identified the fault in the Linux kernel HDA Intel sound driver that causes it to fail after suspend/resume.

### Bug Location
- **File**: `sound/pci/hda/hda_intel.c`
- **Function**: `azx_init_chip()` (lines 1209-1230)
- **Confidence**: 95%

### Root Cause

When a codec communication timeout occurs, the driver sets `chip->single_cmd = 1` as a fallback mode (line 951). During suspend, `azx_stop_chip()` clears the `initialized` flag but **does not reset** the `single_cmd` flag. On resume, `azx_init_chip()` checks `if (!chip->single_cmd)` before reinitializing the CORB/RIRB command I/O (line 1222). Since `single_cmd` is still 1, the CORB/RIRB initialization is **skipped**, leaving the driver in an inconsistent state with the hardware reset but the software still thinking it's in single-command mode.

### Execution Trace
1. **Before suspend**: Timeout → `chip->single_cmd = 1` (line 951)
2. **During suspend**: `azx_stop_chip()` clears `chip->initialized = 0` but not `single_cmd`
3. **During resume**: `azx_init_chip()` called, checks `if (!chip->single_cmd)` → FALSE
4. **Result**: CORB/RIRB not reinitialized → codec communication fails → timeouts and error messages

### Required Fix
Reset the software state flags in `azx_init_chip()` immediately after calling `azx_reset()`:
```c
azx_reset(chip, full_reset);
chip->single_cmd = 0;
chip->polling_mode = 0;
chip->poll_count = 0;
```

The fault localization result has been written to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json`.

When a codec communication timeout occurs, the driver sets chip->single_cmd=1 as a fallback mode (line 951). During suspend, azx_stop_chip() clears chip->initialized=0 but does not reset the single_cmd flag. On resume, azx_init_chip() is called and checks 'if (!chip->single_cmd)' before reinitializing CORB/RIRB (line 1222). Since single_cmd is still 1, the CORB/RIRB command I/O is skipped, leaving the driver in an inconsistent state with hardware reset but software in single_cmd mode. This causes subsequent codec communication timeouts and the error messages observed. The fix is to reset the single_cmd, polling_mode, and poll_count flags immediately after calling azx_reset() in azx_init_chip(), ensuring that after a hardware reset, the driver returns to normal CORB/RIRB mode. This is a regression introduced between kernel 3.6.11 and 3.7.1 where these software state flags were not properly managed across suspend/resume cycles.\"\n}\n",

        Code Changes (3)
        
1. WRITE /logs/agent/sessions/projects/-workspace/memory/MEMORY.md
# Linux HDA Intel Suspend/Resume Bug Investigation

## Bug Summary
- Kernel 3.7.6: Sound stops working after suspend to RAM (regression from 3.6.11)
- Error messages: azx_get_response timeouts, polling mode switch, MSI disable, single_cmd mode
- Sound becomes choppy with clicks and silences

## Key Files
- `sound/pci/hda/hda_intel.c`: Main HDA Intel driver

## Current Analysis
1. **Suspend sequence** (azx_suspend):
   - Calls azx_stop_chip which sets chip->initialized = 0
   - Disables CORB/RIRB via azx_free_cmd_io

2. **Resume sequence** (azx_resume):
   - Restores PCI state
   - Re-enables PCI device and MSI
   - Calls azx_init_chip(chip, 1)

3. **Potential Issue Identified**:
   - Software flags `polling_mode` and `single_cmd` are NOT reset during resume
   - azx_init_chip checks `if (!chip->single_cmd)` before reinitializing CORB/RIRB
   - If single_cmd was set to 1 before suspend, CORB/RIRB won't be reinitialized after resume
   - This causes codec communication to fail

## Next Steps
- Find where polling_mode and single_cmd should be reset
- Check if initialization order or flag clearing changed between 3.6.11 and 3.7.1

2. WRITE /workspace/fault_localization_result.json
{
  "buggy_files": [
    "sound/pci/hda/hda_intel.c"
  ],
  "buggy_functions": [
    "azx_init_chip"
  ],
  "confidence": 0.95,
  "reasoning": "The bug occurs because software state flags (single_cmd and polling_mode) are not reset after a hardware reset during resume. When a codec communication timeout occurs, the driver sets chip->single_cmd=1 as a fallback mode (line 951). During suspend, azx_stop_chip() clears chip->initialized=0 but does not reset the single_cmd flag. On resume, azx_init_chip() is called and checks 'if (!chip->single_cmd)' before reinitializing CORB/RIRB (line 1222). Since single_cmd is still 1, the CORB/RIRB command I/O is skipped, leaving the driver in an inconsistent state with hardware reset but software in single_cmd mode. This causes subsequent codec communication timeouts and the error messages observed. The fix is to reset the single_cmd, polling_mode, and poll_count flags immediately after calling azx_reset() in azx_init_chip(), ensuring that after a hardware reset, the driver returns to normal CORB/RIRB mode. This is a regression introduced between kernel 3.6.11 and 3.7.1 where these software state flags were not properly managed across suspend/resume cycles."
}

3. EDIT /logs/agent/sessions/projects/-workspace/memory/MEMORY.md
Before
## Next Steps
- Find where polling_mode and single_cmd should be reset
- Check if initialization order or flag clearing changed between 3.6.11 and 3.7.1
After
## BUG IDENTIFIED (CONFIRMED)

**Root Cause:** Software state flags (`single_cmd` and `polling_mode`) are not reset during hardware reset on resume

**Execution Flow:**
1. Timeout occurs → azx_rirb_get_response (line 951) sets `chip->single_cmd = 1`
2. Suspend → azx_suspend calls azx_stop_chip which sets `chip->initialized = 0` (line 2448)
3. BUT `chip->single_cmd` remains 1 (not reset in azx_stop_chip)
4. Resume → azx_init_chip (line 2561) is called
5. azx_init_chip checks `if (!chip->single_cmd)` before calling azx_init_cmd_io (line 1222)
6. Since `single_cmd = 1`, CORB/RIRB initialization is SKIPPED
7. Result: Hardware reset but driver stuck in single_cmd mode → codec communication fails

**Fix Location:** `sound/pci/hda/hda_intel.c`, function `azx_init_chip`, after line 1215

**Required Change:** Reset flags immediately after azx_reset:
- `chip->single_cmd = 0;`
- `chip->polling_mode = 0;`
- `chip->poll_count = 0;`

This ensures after hardware reset, driver returns to normal CORB/RIRB mode
